d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003col dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eCaller ↔ axios.\u003c/strong\u003e The caller is fully trusted. Anything the caller passes in \u003ccode\u003econfig\u003c/code\u003e is assumed intentional. axios does \u003cstrong\u003enot\u003c/strong\u003e defend against a malicious caller - that is a non-goal.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eaxios ↔ network.\u003c/strong\u003e Everything past the socket is untrusted: response status, headers, body, redirect \u003ccode\u003eLocation\u003c/code\u003e, proxy responses.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eaxios ↔ environment variables.\u003c/strong\u003e \u003ccode\u003eHTTP_PROXY\u003c/code\u003e / \u003ccode\u003eHTTPS_PROXY\u003c/code\u003e / \u003ccode\u003eNO_PROXY\u003c/code\u003e are read by \u003ccode\u003eproxy-from-env\u003c/code\u003e. An attacker who controls the environment can redirect all traffic. This is treated as trusted (same privilege as the process), but is a relevant pivot in container-escape and CI scenarios.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eCaller-supplied hooks ↔ axios internals.\u003c/strong\u003e Interceptors, \u003ccode\u003etransformRequest\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003etransformResponse\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003eparamsSerializer\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003ebeforeRedirect\u003c/code\u003e, custom adapters. These run with full process privilege. axios does not sandbox them.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ol\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e2.4 Threat Actors\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-24-threat-actors\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: 2.4 Threat Actors\" href=\"#24-threat-actors\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cmarkdown-accessiblity-table\u003e\u003ctable\u003e\n\u003cthead\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003cth\u003eActor\u003c/th\u003e\n\u003cth\u003eCapability\u003c/th\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003c/thead\u003e\n\u003ctbody\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eMalicious server\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eControls every byte of the response. Most common.\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eOn-path network attacker\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eMITM. Mitigated by TLS unless the caller disabled validation.\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eMalicious redirect target\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eA trusted server redirects to an attacker - attacker now sees whatever axios forwards.\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eApplication user\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eControls \u003cem\u003epart\u003c/em\u003e of the request (e.g. a URL path segment, a query param, a header value) via the calling application.\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003c/tbody\u003e\n\u003c/table\u003e\u003c/markdown-accessiblity-table\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e2.5 Threats\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-25-threats\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: 2.5 Threats\" href=\"#25-threats\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cblockquote\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eSeverity\u003c/strong\u003e = Likelihood × Impact, rated for a \u003cem\u003etypical\u003c/em\u003e server-side deployment. This is documented as caller responsibility.\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003c/tbody\u003e\n\u003c/table\u003e\u003c/markdown-accessiblity-table\u003e\n\u003chr\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch4 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eT-R2: Credential leakage on cross-origin redirect\u003c/h4\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-t-r2-credential-leakage-on-cross-origin-redirect\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: T-R2: Credential leakage on cross-origin redirect\" href=\"#t-r2-credential-leakage-on-cross-origin-redirect\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cmarkdown-accessiblity-table\u003e\u003ctable\u003e\n\u003cthead\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003cth\u003e\u003c/th\u003e\n\u003cth\u003e\u003c/th\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003c/thead\u003e\n\u003ctbody\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eDescription\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eCaller sets \u003ccode\u003eAuthorization: Bearer …\u003c/code\u003e and requests \u003ccode\u003ehttps://api.trusted.com/x\u003c/code\u003e. Server responds \u003ccode\u003e302 Location: https://evil.com/\u003c/code\u003e. Does the bearer token go to evil.com?\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eLikelihood\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eMedium\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eImpact\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eHigh (full credential theft)\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eMitigations\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e• Node adapter delegates to \u003ccode\u003efollow-redirects@^1.15.11\u003c/code\u003e, which strips \u003ccode\u003eAuthorization\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003eCookie\u003c/code\u003e, and \u003ccode\u003eProxy-Authorization\u003c/code\u003e on cross-host redirects and on HTTPS→HTTP downgrades. \u003cbr\u003e• \u003ccode\u003emaxRedirects\u003c/code\u003e defaults to 5; set to \u003ccode\u003e0\u003c/code\u003e to handle redirects manually. \u003cbr\u003e• \u003ccode\u003ebeforeRedirect\u003c/code\u003e callback allows custom inspection. \u003cbr\u003e• Browser adapters (XHR/fetch) delegate to the browser, which applies its own cross-origin credential rules.\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eResidual risk\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eLow. We inherit \u003ccode\u003efollow-redirects\u003c/code\u003e' security posture - it is a critical transitive dependency and its CVEs are our CVEs.\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003c/tbody\u003e\n\u003c/table\u003e\u003c/markdown-accessiblity-table\u003e\n\u003chr\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch4 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eT-R3: Header injection (CRLF)\u003c/h4\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-t-r3-header-injection-crlf\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: T-R3: Header injection (CRLF)\" href=\"#t-r3-header-injection-crlf\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cmarkdown-accessiblity-table\u003e\u003ctable\u003e\n\u003cthead\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003cth\u003e\u003c/th\u003e\n\u003cth\u003e\u003c/th\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003c/thead\u003e\n\u003ctbody\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eDescription\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eApplication puts user input into a header value: \u003ccode\u003eheaders: { 'X-User': req.query.name }\u003c/code\u003e. \u003ccode\u003econfig.headers.Authorization\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003econfig.httpsAgent\u003c/code\u003e (with embedded client cert/key). Caller logs the error → secrets in logs.\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eLikelihood\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eHigh\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eImpact\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eMedium–High\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eMitigations\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003eAxiosError.toJSON()\u003c/code\u003e (\u003ccode\u003elib/core/AxiosError.js\u003c/code\u003e) produces a reduced view, but the live error object still carries the full config by reference.\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eResidual risk\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eMedium.\u003c/strong\u003e Callers using structured loggers that walk object graphs (Winston, Pino with serializers, Sentry) will capture credentials unless they configure redaction. This is a documented sharp edge, not a vulnerability - but it is the most common way axios users leak secrets in practice.\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003c/tbody\u003e\n\u003c/table\u003e\u003c/markdown-accessiblity-table\u003e\n\u003chr\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch4 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eT-R9: Proxy environment variable hijack\u003c/h4\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-t-r9-proxy-environment-variable-hijack\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: T-R9: Proxy environment variable hijack\" href=\"#t-r9-proxy-environment-variable-hijack\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cmarkdown-accessiblity-table\u003e\u003ctable\u003e\n\u003cthead\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003cth\u003e\u003c/th\u003e\n\u003cth\u003e\u003c/th\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003c/thead\u003e\n\u003ctbody\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eDescription\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eAttacker controls the process environment (compromised CI step, container escape, \u003ccode\u003e.env\u003c/code\u003e injection) and sets \u003ccode\u003eHTTPS_PROXY=http://evil.com:8080\u003c/code\u003e. All axios traffic is now MITM'd.\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eLikelihood\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eLow (requires prior (\u003ccode\u003elib/helpers/shouldBypassProxy.js\u003c/code\u003e). \u003cbr\u003e• HTTPS through an HTTP proxy still validates the origin's cert (CONNECT tunnel) - the proxy sees SNI but not plaintext.\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eResidual risk\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eLow for HTTPS. \u003cstrong\u003eHigh for plain HTTP\u003c/strong\u003e - the proxy sees and can modify \u003cstrong\u003enot\u003c/strong\u003e:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eSandbox or validate caller-supplied functions (interceptors, transforms, adapters, serializers).\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eValidate that \u003ccode\u003econfig.url\u003c/code\u003e points somewhere \"safe.\" We don't know what safe means for your application.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eWarn when TLS validation is disabled via a custom agent.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eRedact \u003ccode\u003econfig\u003c/code\u003e from thrown errors - secrets\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eSSH keys (→ GitHub push), \u003ccode\u003e~/.npmrc\u003c/code\u003e token if present (→ direct publish), GPG keys (→ signed commits), cloud creds (→ lateral movement).\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eBuild determinism\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eIf \u003ccode\u003edist/\u003c/code\u003e doesn't match \u003ccode\u003elib/\u003c/code\u003e, a backdoor can hide in the minified bundle.\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eRuntime dependency integrity\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003efollow-redirects\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003eform-data\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003eproxy-from-env\u003c/code\u003e ship inside every axios install.\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003c/tbody\u003e\n\u003c/table\u003e\u003c/markdown-accessiblity-table\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e3.3 Trust Boundaries\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-33-trust-boundaries\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: 3.3 Trust Boundaries\" href=\"#33-trust-boundaries\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003col dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eContributor PRs ↔ main branch.\u003c/strong\u003e PRs from forks are untrusted. CI runs them, but \u003ccode\u003epull_request\u003c/code\u003e workflows have no access to secrets and read-only \u003ccode\u003eGITHUB_TOKEN\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eMain branch ↔ release tag.\u003c/strong\u003e Pushing to \u003ccode\u003ev1.x\u003c/code\u003e does not publish. Only pushing a \u003ccode\u003ev1.*.*\u003c/code\u003e \u003cstrong\u003etag\u003c/strong\u003e does. Tag push requires write access.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eGitHub Actions ↔ npm.\u003c/strong\u003e Crossed via OIDC (\u003ccode\u003eid-token: write\u003c/code\u003e → npm trusted publisher). No long-lived \u003ccode\u003eNPM_TOKEN\u003c/code\u003e secret in the repo.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eMaintainer workstation ↔ everything else.\u003c/strong\u003e This is the softest boundary. A maintainer's laptop is a high-value, low-assurance environment. \u003cstrong\u003eSee §3.5.\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ol\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e3.4 Threat Actors\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-34-threat-actors\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: 3.4 Threat Actors\" href=\"#34-threat-actors\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cmarkdown-accessiblity-table\u003e\u003ctable\u003e\n\u003cthead\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003cth\u003eActor\u003c/th\u003e\n\u003cth\u003eCapability\u003c/th\u003e\n\u003cth\u003eMotivation\u003c/th\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003c/thead\u003e\n\u003ctbody\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eDrive-by contributor\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eOpen a PR. No secrets, no write.\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eSneak a backdoor past review.\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eCompromised dependency\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eRun code on \u003ccode\u003enpm install\u003c/code\u003e (lifecycle scripts) on every machine that installs it - including maintainers' and CI.\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eSteal tokens, inject into build.\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003ePhisher\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eSend convincing emails/DMs. No technical access.\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eMaintainer GitHub/npm credential theft.\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eCompromised maintainer account\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eFull write. Can push tags. Can edit workflows.\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eDirect publish of malware.\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eGitHub / npm insider or platform compromise\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eOut of scope. We trust the platforms.\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e-\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003c/tbody\u003e\n\u003c/table\u003e\u003c/markdown-accessiblity-table\u003e\n\u003cdiv opens a PR with a subtle backdoor - an obfuscated payload in a test fixture, a Unicode homoglyph in a comparison, a malicious \u003ccode\u003erollup\u003c/code\u003e plugin in the config.\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eLikelihood\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eHigh\u003c/strong\u003e (attempts are constant on high-profile repos)\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eImpact\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eCritical, \u003cem\u003eif\u003c/em\u003e it lands\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eMitigations\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e• Mandatory review before merge. \u003cbr\u003e• \u003ccode\u003epull_request\u003c/code\u003e workflows run with no secrets and a read-only token - a malicious test cannot exfiltrate anything from CI. \u003cbr\u003e• \u003ccode\u003epull_request_target\u003c/code\u003e is \u003cstrong\u003enot\u003c/strong\u003e used (it would grant secrets to fork code). \u003cbr\u003e• \u003ccode\u003ezizmor\u003c/code\u003e lints workflow files for known-dangerous patterns. \u003cbr\u003e• Branch protection on \u003ccode\u003ev1.x\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eGaps\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e• Review is human and fallible. Obfuscated changes to \u003ccode\u003edist/\u003c/code\u003e (if checked in) or to large test fixtures are hard to spot. \u003cbr\u003e• No automated diffing of \u003ccode\u003elib/\u003c/code\u003e → \u003ccode\u003edist/\u003c/code\u003e to catch build-output tampering. \u003cbr\u003e• No \u003ccode\u003eCODEOWNERS\u003c/code\u003e requiring specific reviewers for \u003ccode\u003elib/\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003e.github/\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003erollup.config.js\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003c/tbody\u003e\n\u003c/table\u003e\u003c/markdown-accessiblity-table\u003e\n\u003chr\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch4 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eT-S2: Compromised dev dependency steals maintainer keys ⚠\u003c/h4\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-t-s2-compromised-dev-dependency-steals-maintainer-keys-\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: T-S2: Compromised dev dependency steals maintainer keys ⚠\" href=\"#t-s2-compromised-dev-dependency-steals-maintainer-keys-\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cblockquote\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eThis is the threat the project is least defended against today.\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/blockquote\u003e\n\u003cmarkdown-accessiblity-table\u003e\u003ctable\u003e\n\u003cthead\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003cth\u003e\u003c/th\u003e\n\u003cth\u003e\u003c/th\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003c/thead\u003e\n\u003ctbody\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eDescription\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eOne of the ~45 direct dev dependencies - or one of their \u003cstrong\u003ethousands\u003c/strong\u003e of transitive dependencies - is compromised (maintainer account takeover, expired domain re-registration, the usual). It ships a \u003ccode\u003epostinstall\u003c/code\u003e script that reads \u003ccode\u003e~/.npmrc\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003e~/.ssh/id_*\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003e~/.config/gh/hosts.yml\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003e~/.aws/credentials\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003e~/.gnupg/\u003c/code\u003e and POSTs them to an attacker. \u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eThe next time a maintainer runs \u003ccode\u003enpm install\u003c/code\u003e on their workstation, the script runs \u003cstrong\u003eas the maintainer's user\u003c/strong\u003e, with full filesystem access. No exploit needed - this is npm working as designed.\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eLikelihood\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eMedium and rising.\u003c/strong\u003e This exact pattern has hit \u003ccode\u003eevent-stream\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003eua-parser-js\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003ecoa\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003erc\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003enode-ipc\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003e@solana/web3.js\u003c/code\u003e, the Ledger connect-kit, the 2024 polyfill.io incident, and dozens more. axios' dev tree includes Babel, Rollup, Gulp, ESLint, Vitest, Playwright - each pulling hundreds of transitives. The attack surface is enormous and refreshes on every \u003ccode\u003enpm install\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eImpact\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eCritical.\u003c/strong\u003e A stolen npm token with publish rights = direct malware publish. A stolen SSH key with GitHub push rights = tag push → publish via CI. Either path ends the same way.\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eCurrent mitigations\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e• \u003cstrong\u003eCI is protected:\u003c/strong\u003e \u003ccode\u003epublish.yml\u003c/code\u003e runs \u003ccode\u003enpm ci --ignore-scripts\u003c/code\u003e, so a malicious lifecycle script cannot execute during the release build. ✅ \u003cbr\u003e• \u003cstrong\u003eCI uses OIDC, not a stored token\u003c/strong\u003e - there is no \u003ccode\u003eNPM_TOKEN\u003c/code\u003e secret in GitHub for a malicious workflow step to steal. ✅ \u003cbr\u003e• \u003ccode\u003epackage-lock.json\u003c/code\u003e pins versions and integrity hashes - a \u003cem\u003enew\u003c/em\u003e malicious version won't arrive silently, only on explicit update. ✅ \u003cbr\u003e• \u003ccode\u003ehusky\u003c/code\u003e is the only \u003ccode\u003eprepare\u003c/code\u003e hook and only writes \u003ccode\u003e.git/hooks/\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eGaps - the workstation\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eNone of the above protects a maintainer running \u003ccode\u003enpm install\u003c/code\u003e \u003cstrong\u003elocally\u003c/strong\u003e. The lockfile pins \u003cem\u003ewhich\u003c/em\u003e packages install, but if one of those pinned packages was \u003cem\u003ealready\u003c/em\u003e malicious when the lock was generated, or if a maintainer runs \u003ccode\u003enpm update\u003c/code\u003e / \u003ccode\u003enpm install \u0026lt;new-pkg\u0026gt;\u003c/code\u003e, the scripts run. \u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eThe development environment has full read access to every credential the maintainer's user can read.\u003c/strong\u003e That's the threat.\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003c/tbody\u003e\n\u003c/table\u003e\u003c/markdown-accessiblity-table\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eMitigations maintainers SHOULD adopt\u003c/strong\u003e (in roughly descending order of effectiveness):\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003col dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eDon't keep a publish-capable npm token on your workstation.\u003c/strong\u003e\nPublishing happens via GitHub Actions OIDC. There is no workflow that requires \u003ccode\u003enpm publish\u003c/code\u003e from a laptop. If \u003ccode\u003e~/.npmrc\u003c/code\u003e has a token, it should be read-only or scoped to unrelated packages. \u003cem\u003eIf there's nothing to steal, the attack is defanged.\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eRun \u003ccode\u003enpm install\u003c/code\u003e / \u003ccode\u003enpm ci\u003c/code\u003e with \u003ccode\u003e--ignore-scripts\u003c/code\u003e locally.\u003c/strong\u003e\nAdd to a project-local \u003ccode\u003e.npmrc\u003c/code\u003e:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"ignore-scripts=true\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eignore-scripts=true\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThen explicitly run the one trusted script you need:\n\u003ccode\u003enpm rebuild husky \u0026amp;\u0026amp; npx husky\u003c/code\u003e. The minor inconvenience of manually running known-good post-install steps is the price of not running thousands of unknown ones.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eDevelop in an isolated environment.\u003c/strong\u003e\nA devcontainer, VM, or sandbox profile that does not have:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003e~/.ssh/\u003c/code\u003e mounted (use a separate deploy key or SSH agent forwarding only when pushing)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003e~/.npmrc\u003c/code\u003e with publish tokens\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003e~/.config/gh/\u003c/code\u003e with a \u003ccode\u003erepo\u003c/code\u003e-scoped GitHub token\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003e~/.aws/\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003e~/.config/gcloud/\u003c/code\u003e, etc.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe dev environment should be able to read/write the repo working tree and reach the network for tests. Nothing else.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eUse hardware-backed keys for GitHub.\u003c/strong\u003e\nFIDO2/WebAuthn for the GitHub account, and \u003ccode\u003esk-ssh-ed25519@openssh.com\u003c/code\u003e for git push. A stolen \u003ccode\u003e~/.ssh/id_ed25519_sk\u003c/code\u003e is useless without the physical key. This converts \"steal a file\" into \"steal a file AND a physical object.\"\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eAudit lockfile diffs on dependency-update PRs as carefully as code.\u003c/strong\u003e\nA 4000-line \u003ccode\u003epackage-lock.json\u003c/code\u003e diff hides a lot. Tooling: \u003ccode\u003enpm diff\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003elockfile-lint\u003c/code\u003e, Socket.dev's PR integration. Pay particular attention to new packages with install scripts (\u003ccode\u003ehasInstallScript: true\u003c/code\u003e in the lockfile).\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eDon't add dev dependencies casually.\u003c/strong\u003e\nEach one is a recurring trust decision delegated to a stranger. Prefer tools that can run via \u003ccode\u003enpx\u003c/code\u003e on demand (not in \u003ccode\u003enode_modules\u003c/code\u003e) or that are already in the tree.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ol\u003e\n\u003chr\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch4 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eT-S3: Phishing → maintainer account takeover\u003c/h4\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-t-s3-phishing--maintainer-account-takeover\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: T-S3: Phishing → maintainer account takeover\" href=\"#t-s3-phishing--maintainer-account-takeover\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 receives a convincing email: \u003cbr\u003e• \"\u003cem\u003enpm security alert: your axios package has been flagged, log in to verify ownership\u003c/em\u003e\" → fake npm login → password + TOTP captured and replayed in real-time. \u003cbr\u003e• \"\u003cem\u003eGitHub: @axios has been added to a new organization, review access\u003c/em\u003e\" → fake GitHub OAuth consent → attacker app gets \u003ccode\u003erepo\u003c/code\u003e scope. \u003cbr\u003e• Social: a \"recruiter\" asks the maintainer to clone and \u003ccode\u003enpm install\u003c/code\u003e a \"take-home assignment\" repo. \u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003enpm and GitHub credentials for axios maintainers have been \u003cem\u003especifically targeted\u003c/em\u003e by these campaigns in the past - this is not theoretical.\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eLikelihood\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eHigh.\u003c/strong\u003e These campaigns are continuous.\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eImpact\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eCritical. GitHub account → push tag → publish. npm account → publish directly.\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eMitigations\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e• npm 2FA is \u003cstrong\u003erequired\u003c/strong\u003e for publish on the \u003ccode\u003eaxios\u003c/code\u003e package. \u003cbr\u003e• But: TOTP 2FA is \u003cstrong\u003ephishable\u003c/strong\u003e via real-time relay (Evilginx, Modlishka). \u003cbr\u003e• OIDC publishing means there's no maintainer npm session involved in a normal release - this \u003cem\u003enarrows\u003c/em\u003e the attack to GitHub. \u003cbr\u003e• GitHub: maintainers should use \u003cstrong\u003eWebAuthn/passkeys\u003c/strong\u003e, which are origin-bound and cannot be relayed by a phishing proxy. TOTP is not sufficient for an account guarding a package this widely deployed.\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eGaps\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e• This is a \u003cem\u003epolicy\u003c/em\u003e control, not enforceable in the repo. The project cannot verify what 2FA method each maintainer uses. \u003cbr\u003e• No documented \"I think I've been phished\" runbook (revoke sessions, rotate keys, audit recent tags, contact npm support).\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003c/tbody\u003e\n\u003c/table\u003e\u003c/markdown-accessiblity-table\u003e\n\u003chr\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch4 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eT-S4: Compromised runtime dependency\u003c/h4\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-t-s4-compromised-runtime-dependency\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: T-S4: Compromised runtime dependency\" href=\"#t-s4-compromised-runtime-dependency\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cmarkdown-accessiblity-table\u003e\u003ctable\u003e\n\u003cthead\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003cth\u003e\u003c/th\u003e\n\u003cth\u003e\u003c/th\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003c/thead\u003e\n\u003ctbody\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eDescription\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003efollow-redirects\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003eform-data\u003c/code\u003e, or \u003ccode\u003eproxy-from-env\u003c/code\u003e ships a malicious version. Unlike T-S2, this code ends up \u003cstrong\u003ein the published axios bundle / runtime\u003c/strong\u003e, not just on maintainer machines. Every axios consumer runs it.\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eLikelihood\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eLow (only 3 deps; all are mature, narrowly-scoped, and watched)\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eImpact\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eCritical\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eMitigations\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e• Three runtime deps total - minimal by design. \u003cbr\u003e• \u003ccode\u003e^\u003c/code\u003e ranges in \u003ccode\u003epackage.json\u003c/code\u003e mean consumers may get newer patch versions than the lockfile pins - this is intentional (consumers get security fixes) but means a malicious patch release of \u003ccode\u003efollow-redirects\u003c/code\u003e propagates without an axios release. \u003cbr\u003e• \u003ccode\u003efollow-redirects\u003c/code\u003e is security-conscious and well-maintained; we track its advisories closely (multiple past axios releases were just \u003ccode\u003efollow-redirects\u003c/code\u003e bumps). \u003cbr\u003e• Dependabot is configured (\u003ccode\u003e.github/dependabot.yml\u003c/code\u003e) for both npm and GitHub Actions, running weekly with grouped updates for production and development dependencies.\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eGaps\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e• No vendoring/inlining considered. The deps are small enough that vendoring is plausible but would forfeit upstream security fixes. Current judgment: not worth it.\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003c/tbody\u003e\n\u003c/table\u003e\u003c/markdown-accessiblity-table\u003e\n\u003chr\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch4 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eT-S5: Build-output tampering (\u003ccode\u003edist/\u003c/code\u003e ≠ \u003ccode\u003elib/\u003c/code\u003e)\u003c/h4\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-t-s5-build-output-tampering-dist--lib\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: T-S5: Build-output tampering (dist/ ≠ lib/)\" href=\"#t-s5-build-output-tampering-dist--lib\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cmarkdown-accessiblity-table\u003e\u003ctable\u003e\n\u003cthead\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003cth\u003e\u003c/th\u003e\n\u003cth\u003e\u003c/th\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003c/thead\u003e\n\u003ctbody\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eDescription\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eThe published tarball contains a \u003ccode\u003edist/axios.min.js\u003c/code\u003e that doesn't match what \u003ccode\u003erollup\u003c/code\u003e would produce from \u003ccode\u003elib/\u003c/code\u003e. Nobody reads minified bundles. A backdoor here is invisible to source review. \u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eVectors: a malicious dev-dep Rollup/Babel/Terser plugin injects code at build time (T-S2 applied to CI), or a maintainer with a compromised workstation accidentally publishes a tampered local build.\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eLikelihood\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eLow\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eImpact\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eCritical\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eMitigations\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e• Builds run \u003cstrong\u003eonly in CI\u003c/strong\u003e as part of \u003ccode\u003epublish.yml\u003c/code\u003e, from a clean \u003ccode\u003enpm ci --ignore-scripts\u003c/code\u003e checkout. There is no \"publish from laptop\" path. ✅ \u003cbr\u003e• \u003ccode\u003e--ignore-scripts\u003c/code\u003e means a malicious dev dep can't tamper with \u003ccode\u003enode_modules\u003c/code\u003e \u003cem\u003ebefore\u003c/em\u003e the build, but it \u003cstrong\u003ecan\u003c/strong\u003e still tamper \u003cem\u003eduring\u003c/em\u003e the build if it's a Rollup/Babel plugin - those run as part of \u003ccode\u003enpm run build\u003c/code\u003e, not as lifecycle scripts. \u003cbr\u003e• npm provenance (\u003ccode\u003e--provenance\u003c/code\u003e) cryptographically attests \u003cem\u003ewhich workflow on which commit\u003c/em\u003e produced the tarball. Consumers can verify with \u003ccode\u003enpm audit signatures\u003c/code\u003e. This proves the build ran in GitHub Actions on a known SHA - it does \u003cstrong\u003enot\u003c/strong\u003e prove the build is correct, only that it's traceable.\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eGaps\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e• The build is not currently \u003cstrong\u003ereproducible\u003c/strong\u003e in the strict sense - a third party cannot independently rebuild and get a byte-identical \u003ccode\u003edist/\u003c/code\u003e. Timestamps, plugin ordering, and minifier nondeterminism would need to be locked down. \u003cbr\u003e• No automated \u003ccode\u003edist/\u003c/code\u003e-vs-rebuild diff in CI. This is the cheapest available improvement.\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003c/tbody\u003e\n\u003c/table\u003e\u003c/markdown-accessiblity-table\u003e\n\u003chr\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch4 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eT-S6: Workflow file tampering\u003c/h4\u003e\u003ca with write access (or a merged PR that wasn't reviewed carefully) modifies \u003ccode\u003e.github/workflows/publish.yml\u003c/code\u003e to also \u003ccode\u003ecurl\u003c/code\u003e the OIDC token somewhere, or to add a step that patches \u003ccode\u003edist/\u003c/code\u003e after the
