  └────────┬────────┘
  ┌────────▼────────┐
  │  Origin server  │  ← UNTRUSTED in the general case
  │  + redirects    │
  └─────────────────┘
</code></pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">2.2 Assets</h3><a id="user-content-22-assets" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: 2.2 Assets" href="#22-assets"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>Asset</th>
<th>Why it matters</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>Credentials in transit</td>
<td><code>config.auth</code>, <code>Authorization</code> headers, cookies, XSRF tokens</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Request/response bodies</td>
<td>May contain PII, business secrets</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>The caller's process integrity</td>
<td>Prototype pollution → RCE in some downstream gadgets</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>The caller's internal network</td>
<td>SSRF can pivot through the host running axios</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Availability</td>
<td>Decompression bombs, redirect loops, slow-loris responses</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">2.3 Trust Boundaries</h3><a id="user-content-23-trust-boundaries" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: 2.3 Trust Boundaries" href="#23-trust-boundaries"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<ol dir="auto">
<li><strong>Caller ↔ axios.</strong> The caller is fully trusted. Anything the caller passes in <code>config</code> is assumed intentional. axios does <strong>not</strong> defend against a malicious caller - that is a non-goal.</li>
<li><strong>axios ↔ network.</strong> Everything past the socket is untrusted: response status, headers, body, redirect <code>Location</code>, proxy responses.</li>
<li><strong>axios ↔ environment variables.</strong> <code>HTTP_PROXY</code> / <code>HTTPS_PROXY</code> / <code>NO_PROXY</code> are read by <code>proxy-from-env</code>. An attacker who controls the environment can redirect all traffic. This is treated as trusted (same privilege as the process), but is a relevant pivot in container-escape and CI scenarios.</li>
<li><strong>Caller-supplied hooks ↔ axios internals.</strong> Interceptors, <code>transformRequest</code>, <code>transformResponse</code>, <code>paramsSerializer</code>, <code>beforeRedirect</code>, custom adapters. These run with full process privilege. axios does not sandbox them.</li>
</ol>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">2.4 Threat Actors</h3><a id="user-content-24-threat-actors" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: 2.4 Threat Actors" href="#24-threat-actors"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>Actor</th>
<th>Capability</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td><strong>Malicious server</strong></td>
<td>Controls every byte of the response. Most common.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>On-path network attacker</strong></td>
<td>MITM. Mitigated by TLS unless the caller disabled validation.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Malicious redirect target</strong></td>
<td>A trusted server redirects to an attacker - attacker now sees whatever axios forwards.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Application user</strong></td>
<td>Controls <em>part</em> of the request (e.g. a URL path segment, a query param, a header value) via the calling application.</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">2.5 Threats</h3><a id="user-content-25-threats" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: 2.5 Threats" href="#25-threats"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<blockquote>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Severity</strong> = Likelihood × Impact, rated for a <em>typical</em> server-side deployment. Browser deployments inherit the browser's same-origin policy and are generally lower risk for SSRF/credential leakage.</p>
</blockquote>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">T-R1: SSRF via caller-controlled URL</h4><a id="user-content-t-r1-ssrf-via-caller-controlled-url" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: T-R1: SSRF via caller-controlled URL" href="#t-r1-ssrf-via-caller-controlled-url"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th></th>
<th></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td><strong>Description</strong></td>
<td>Application interpolates user input into <code>config.url</code> or <code>config.baseURL</code>. Attacker supplies <code>http://169.254.169.254/</code>, <code>http://localhost:6379/</code>, <code>file://</code>, <code>gopher://</code>, etc.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Likelihood</strong></td>
<td><strong>High</strong> - this is the #1 real-world axios misuse pattern.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Impact</strong></td>
<td><strong>High</strong> - cloud metadata theft, internal service access.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>In scope?</strong></td>
<td><strong>Partially.</strong> axios cannot know which URLs the caller intends to allow.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Mitigations</strong></td>
<td>• <code>allowAbsoluteUrls: false</code> prevents a relative <code>url</code> from overriding <code>baseURL</code> (<code>lib/core/buildFullPath.js</code>). Defaults to <code>true</code> for back-compat. <br>• The HTTP adapter only speaks <code>http:</code>/<code>https:</code>/<code>file:</code>/<code>data:</code> (Node) or <code>http:</code>/<code>https:</code>/<code>file:</code>/<code>blob:</code>/<code>url:</code>/<code>data:</code> (browser) - exotic schemes like <code>gopher:</code> are rejected (<code>lib/platform/node/index.js</code>, <code>lib/platform/browser/index.js</code>). <br>• <strong>No built-in host allowlist.</strong> Callers MUST validate destinations themselves.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Residual risk</strong></td>
<td>Substantial. This is documented as caller responsibility.</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">T-R2: Credential leakage on cross-origin redirect</h4><a id="user-content-t-r2-credential-leakage-on-cross-origin-redirect" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: T-R2: Credential leakage on cross-origin redirect" href="#t-r2-credential-leakage-on-cross-origin-redirect"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th></th>
<th></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td><strong>Description</strong></td>
<td>Caller sets <code>Authorization: Bearer …</code> and requests <code>https://api.trusted.com/x</code>. Server responds <code>302 Location: https://evil.com/</code>. Does the bearer token go to evil.com?</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Likelihood</strong></td>
<td>Medium</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Impact</strong></td>
<td>High (full credential theft)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Mitigations</strong></td>
<td>• Node adapter delegates to <code>follow-redirects@^1.15.11</code>, which strips <code>Authorization</code>, <code>Cookie</code>, and <code>Proxy-Authorization</code> on cross-host redirects and on HTTPS→HTTP downgrades. <br>• <code>maxRedirects</code> defaults to 5; set to <code>0</code> to handle redirects manually. <br>• <code>beforeRedirect</code> callback allows custom inspection. <br>• Browser adapters (XHR/fetch) delegate to the browser, which applies its own cross-origin credential rules.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Residual risk</strong></td>
<td>Low. We inherit <code>follow-redirects</code>' security posture - it is a critical transitive dependency and its CVEs are our CVEs.</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">T-R3: Header injection (CRLF)</h4><a id="user-content-t-r3-header-injection-crlf" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: T-R3: Header injection (CRLF)" href="#t-r3-header-injection-crlf"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th></th>
<th></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td><strong>Description</strong></td>
<td>Application puts user input into a header value: <code>headers: { 'X-User': req.query.name }</code>. Attacker supplies <code>foo\r\nX-Injected: bar\r\n\r\n&lt;body&gt;</code>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Likelihood</strong></td>
<td>Low</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Impact</strong></td>
<td>Medium–High (request smuggling, response splitting)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Mitigations</strong></td>
<td><code>lib/core/AxiosHeaders.js</code> rejects header values containing <code>\r</code> or <code>\n</code>, and validates header names against an RFC-7230-shaped charset. Node's own <code>http</code> module also rejects these.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Residual risk</strong></td>
<td>Very low. Defense in depth (axios + Node).</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">T-R4: Prototype pollution via response body</h4><a id="user-content-t-r4-prototype-pollution-via-response-body" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: T-R4: Prototype pollution via response body" href="#t-r4-prototype-pollution-via-response-body"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th></th>
<th></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td><strong>Description</strong></td>
<td>Server returns <code>{"__proto__": {"isAdmin": true}}</code>. If axios merged this into an object naively, every <code>{}</code> in the process would gain <code>.isAdmin</code>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Likelihood</strong></td>
<td>Low (requires a downstream gadget to be exploitable)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Impact</strong></td>
<td>High (process-wide state corruption, sometimes RCE)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Mitigations</strong></td>
<td>• <code>JSON.parse</code> itself does not pollute (it creates own-properties named <code>__proto__</code>, not prototype links). <br>• Internal merge paths filter dangerous keys: <code>lib/utils.js</code> and <code>lib/core/mergeConfig.js</code> filter <code>__proto__</code> / <code>constructor</code> / <code>prototype</code>; <code>lib/helpers/formDataToJSON.js</code> filters <code>__proto__</code>. <br>• These were added in response to past advisories - regression here is a P0.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Residual risk</strong></td>
<td>Low, but this is an area of active attacker interest. New merge helpers MUST go through the same filtering.</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">T-R5: Decompression bomb</h4><a id="user-content-t-r5-decompression-bomb" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: T-R5: Decompression bomb" href="#t-r5-decompression-bomb"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th></th>
<th></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td><strong>Description</strong></td>
<td>Server sends <code>Content-Encoding: gzip</code> with a 10 KB body that decompresses to 10 GB.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Likelihood</strong></td>
<td>Low</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Impact</strong></td>
<td>Medium (DoS - OOM kill of the calling process)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Mitigations</strong></td>
<td>• <code>maxContentLength</code> bounds the <strong>decompressed</strong> response size in the Node adapter (<code>lib/adapters/http.js</code>). <br>• <code>maxBodyLength</code> bounds the request side. <br>• Both default to <code>-1</code> (unlimited). <strong>Callers handling untrusted servers should set these.</strong> <br>• Decompression uses Node's <code>zlib</code>, which streams - memory is bounded by the limit, not the full expansion.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Residual risk</strong></td>
<td>Medium when limits are not configured. The defaults favor compatibility over safety.</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">T-R6: TLS validation bypass</h4><a id="user-content-t-r6-tls-validation-bypass" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: T-R6: TLS validation bypass" href="#t-r6-tls-validation-bypass"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th></th>
<th></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td><strong>Description</strong></td>
<td>Caller passes <code>httpsAgent: new https.Agent({ rejectUnauthorized: false })</code> to "fix" a certificate error in dev, ships it to prod.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Likelihood</strong></td>
<td>Medium (very common copy-paste anti-pattern)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Impact</strong></td>
<td>High (silent MITM)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>In scope?</strong></td>
<td><strong>No.</strong> axios delegates TLS entirely to Node's <code>https</code> module / the browser. We do not inspect or warn on agent configuration.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Mitigations</strong></td>
<td>None at the axios layer. Documentation responsibility only.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Residual risk</strong></td>
<td>High, but explicitly out of scope. This is caller misconfiguration, not an axios vulnerability.</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">T-R7: XSRF token sent cross-origin</h4><a id="user-content-t-r7-xsrf-token-sent-cross-origin" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: T-R7: XSRF token sent cross-origin" href="#t-r7-xsrf-token-sent-cross-origin"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th></th>
<th></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td><strong>Description</strong></td>
<td>Browser deployment. <code>xsrfCookieName</code> is set; attacker tricks the app into requesting <code>https://evil.com</code> and the XSRF token cookie value is attached as a header.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Likelihood</strong></td>
<td>Low</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Impact</strong></td>
<td>Medium</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Mitigations</strong></td>
<td><code>lib/helpers/resolveConfig.js</code> only attaches the XSRF header when <code>isURLSameOrigin()</code> passes (or when <code>withXSRFToken</code> is explicitly forced). This was the fix for <strong>CVE-2023-45857</strong>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Residual risk</strong></td>
<td>Low. The same-origin check uses the WHATWG <code>URL</code> parser (<code>lib/helpers/isURLSameOrigin.js</code>), which is robust against parser-differential attacks.</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">T-R8: Sensitive data in error objects</h4><a id="user-content-t-r8-sensitive-data-in-error-objects" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: T-R8: Sensitive data in error objects" href="#t-r8-sensitive-data-in-error-objects"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th></th>
<th></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td><strong>Description</strong></td>
<td>Request fails. <code>AxiosError</code> includes <code>config</code>, which includes <code>config.auth</code>, <code>config.headers.Authorization</code>, <code>config.httpsAgent</code> (with embedded client cert/key). Caller logs the error → secrets in logs.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Likelihood</strong></td>
<td><strong>High</strong></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Impact</strong></td>
<td>Medium–High</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Mitigations</strong></td>
<td><code>AxiosError.toJSON()</code> (<code>lib/core/AxiosError.js</code>) produces a reduced view, but the live error object still carries the full config by reference.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Residual risk</strong></td>
<td><strong>Medium.</strong> Callers using structured loggers that walk object graphs (Winston, Pino with serializers, Sentry) will capture credentials unless they configure redaction. This is a documented sharp edge, not a vulnerability - but it is the most common way axios users leak secrets in practice.</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">T-R9: Proxy environment variable hijack</h4><a id="user-content-t-r9-proxy-environment-variable-hijack" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: T-R9: Proxy environment variable hijack" href="#t-r9-proxy-environment-variable-hijack"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th></th>
<th></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td><strong>Description</strong></td>
<td>Attacker controls the process environment (compromised CI step, container escape, <code>.env</code> injection) and sets <code>HTTPS_PROXY=http://evil.com:8080</code>. All axios traffic is now MITM'd.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Likelihood</strong></td>
<td>Low (requires prior foothold)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Impact</strong></td>
<td>High</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Mitigations</strong></td>
<td>• <code>config.proxy: false</code> disables environment-based proxy detection entirely. <br>• <code>NO_PROXY</code> is honored (<code>lib/helpers/shouldBypassProxy.js</code>). <br>• HTTPS through an HTTP proxy still validates the origin's cert (CONNECT tunnel) - the proxy sees SNI but not plaintext.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Residual risk</strong></td>
<td>Low for HTTPS. <strong>High for plain HTTP</strong> - the proxy sees and can modify everything.</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">T-R10: Malicious interceptor / adapter</h4><a id="user-content-t-r10-malicious-interceptor--adapter" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: T-R10: Malicious interceptor / adapter" href="#t-r10-malicious-interceptor--adapter"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th></th>
<th></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td><strong>Description</strong></td>
<td>Caller installs a third-party "axios plugin" from npm that registers an interceptor exfiltrating every <code>Authorization</code> header.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Likelihood</strong></td>
<td>Low–Medium</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Impact</strong></td>
<td>High</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>In scope?</strong></td>
<td><strong>No.</strong> Interceptors are caller-supplied code running in the caller's process. axios provides the hook; vetting what goes into it is the caller's job.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Residual risk</strong></td>
<td>Out of scope, but worth documenting: there is no meaningful difference between <code>axios.interceptors.request.use(evil)</code> and <code>require('evil')</code>.</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">2.6 Explicit Non-Goals (Runtime)</h3><a id="user-content-26-explicit-non-goals-runtime" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: 2.6 Explicit Non-Goals (Runtime)" href="#26-explicit-non-goals-runtime"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">axios will <strong>not</strong>:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Sandbox or validate caller-supplied functions (interceptors, transforms, adapters, serializers).</li>
<li>Validate that <code>config.url</code> points somewhere "safe." We don't know what safe means for your application.</li>
<li>Warn when TLS validation is disabled via a custom agent.</li>
<li>Redact <code>config</code> from thrown errors - the caller may legitimately need it for retry logic.</li>
<li>Defend against a caller that has already been compromised (e.g. polluted <code>Object.prototype</code> before calling axios).</li>
</ul>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">3. Project / Supply-Chain Threat Model</h2><a id="user-content-3-project--supply-chain-threat-model" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: 3. Project / Supply-Chain Threat Model" href="#3-project--supply-chain-threat-model"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">This is the model that protects <strong>what gets published as <code>axios</code> on npm</strong>. A successful attack here compromises every downstream consumer simultaneously. Given axios' install base, this is the higher-stakes half of the document.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">3.1 System Overview</h3><a id="user-content-31-system-overview" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: 3.1 System Overview" href="#31-system-overview"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>

<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">3.2 Assets</h3><a id="user-content-32-assets" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: 3.2 Assets" href="#32-assets"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>Asset</th>
<th>Compromise means…</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td><strong>The npm <code>axios</code> package name</strong></td>
<td>Attacker can publish malware as <code>axios@1.x.y+1</code>. Game over for the ecosystem.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>npm publish capability</strong></td>
<td>Whether via token, OIDC trust, or account takeover.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>GitHub <code>axios/axios</code> write access</strong></td>
<td>Attacker can push a tag → triggers publish. Or modify <code>publish.yml</code> itself.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Maintainer GitHub accounts</strong></td>
<td>Transitively grants the above.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Maintainer workstation secrets</strong></td>
<td>SSH keys (→ GitHub push), <code>~/.npmrc</code> token if present (→ direct publish), GPG keys (→ signed commits), cloud creds (→ lateral movement).</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Build determinism</strong></td>
<td>If <code>dist/</code> doesn't match <code>lib/</code>, a backdoor can hide in the minified bundle.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Runtime dependency integrity</strong></td>
<td><code>follow-redirects</code>, <code>form-data</code>, <code>proxy-from-env</code> ship inside every axios install.</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">3.3 Trust Boundaries</h3><a id="user-content-33-trust-boundaries" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: 3.3 Trust Boundaries" href="#33-trust-boundaries"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<ol dir="auto">
<li><strong>Contributor PRs ↔ main branch.</strong> PRs from forks are untrusted. CI runs them, but <code>pull_request</code> workflows have no access to secrets and read-only <code>GITHUB_TOKEN</code>.</li>
<li><strong>Main branch ↔ release tag.</strong> Pushing to <code>v1.x</code> does not publish. Only pushing a <code>v1.*.*</code> <strong>tag</strong> does. Tag push requires write access.</li>
<li><strong>GitHub Actions ↔ npm.</strong> Crossed via OIDC (<code>id-token: write</code> → npm trusted publisher). No long-lived <code>NPM_TOKEN</code> secret in the repo.</li>
<li><strong>Maintainer workstation ↔ everything else.</strong> This is the softest boundary. A maintainer's laptop is a high-value, low-assurance environment. <strong>See §3.5.</strong></li>
</ol>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">3.4 Threat Actors</h3><a id="user-content-34-threat-actors" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: 3.4 Threat Actors" href="#34-threat-actors"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>Actor</th>
<th>Capability</th>
<th>Motivation</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td><strong>Drive-by contributor</strong></td>
<td>Open a PR. No secrets, no write.</td>
<td>Sneak a backdoor past review.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Compromised dependency</strong></td>
<td>Run code on <code>npm install</code> (lifecycle scripts) on every machine that installs it - including maintainers' and CI.</td>
<td>Steal tokens, inject into build.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Phisher</strong></td>
<td>Send convincing emails/DMs. No technical access.</td>
<td>Maintainer GitHub/npm credential theft.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Compromised maintainer account</strong></td>
<td>Full write. Can push tags. Can edit workflows.</td>
<td>Direct publish of malware.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>GitHub / npm insider or platform compromise</strong></td>
<td>Out of scope. We trust the platforms.</td>
<td>-</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">3.5 Threats</h3><a id="user-content-35-threats" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: 3.5 Threats" href="#35-threats"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">T-S1: Malicious code in a contributor PR</h4><a id="user-content-t-s1-malicious-code-in-a-contributor-pr" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: T-S1: Malicious code in a contributor PR" href="#t-s1-malicious-code-in-a-contributor-pr"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th></th>
<th></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td><strong>Description</strong></td>
<td>Attacker opens a PR with a subtle backdoor - an obfuscated payload in a test fixture, a Unicode homoglyph in a comparison, a malicious <code>rollup</code> plugin in the config.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Likelihood</strong></td>
<td><strong>High</strong> (attempts are constant on high-profile repos)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Impact</strong></td>
<td>Critical, <em>if</em> it lands</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Mitigations</strong></td>
<td>• Mandatory review before merge. <br>• <code>pull_request</code> workflows run with no secrets and a read-only token - a malicious test cannot exfiltrate anything from CI. <br>• <code>pull_request_target</code> is <strong>not</strong> used (it would grant secrets to fork code). <br>• <code>zizmor</code> lints workflow files for known-dangerous patterns. <br>• Branch protection on <code>v1.x</code>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Gaps</strong></td>
<td>• Review is human and fallible. Obfuscated changes to <code>dist/</code> (if checked in) or to large test fixtures are hard to spot. <br>• No automated diffing of <code>lib/</code> → <code>dist/</code> to catch build-output tampering. <br>• No <code>CODEOWNERS</code> requiring specific reviewers for <code>lib/</code>, <code>.github/</code>, <code>rollup.config.js</code>.</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">T-S2: Compromised dev dependency steals maintainer keys ⚠</h4><a id="user-content-t-s2-compromised-dev-dependency-steals-maintainer-keys-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: T-S2: Compromised dev dependency steals maintainer keys ⚠" href="#t-s2-compromised-dev-dependency-steals-maintainer-keys-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<blockquote>
<p dir="auto"><strong>This is the threat the project is least defended against today.</strong></p>
</blockquote>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th></th>
<th></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td><strong>Description</strong></td>
<td>One of the ~45 direct dev dependencies - or one of their <strong>thousands</strong> of transitive dependencies - is compromised (maintainer account takeover, expired domain re-registration, the usual). It ships a <code>postinstall</code> script that reads <code>~/.npmrc</code>, <code>~/.ssh/id_*</code>, <code>~/.config/gh/hosts.yml</code>, <code>~/.aws/credentials</code>, <code>~/.gnupg/</code> and POSTs them to an attacker. <br><br>The next time a maintainer runs <code>npm install</code> on their workstation, the script runs <strong>as the maintainer's user</strong>, with full filesystem access. No exploit needed - this is npm working as designed.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Likelihood</strong></td>
<td><strong>Medium and rising.</strong> This exact pattern has hit <code>event-stream</code>, <code>ua-parser-js</code>, <code>coa</code>, <code>rc</code>, <code>node-ipc</code>, <code>@solana/web3.js</code>, the Ledger connect-kit, the 2024 polyfill.io incident, and dozens more. axios' dev tree includes Babel, Rollup, Gulp, ESLint, Vitest, Playwright - each pulling hundreds of transitives. The attack surface is enormous and refreshes on every <code>npm install</code>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Impact</strong></td>
<td><strong>Critical.</strong> A stolen npm token with publish rights = direct malware publish. A stolen SSH key with GitHub push rights = tag push → publish via CI. Either path ends the same way.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Current mitigations</strong></td>
<td>• <strong>CI is protected:</strong> <code>publish.yml</code> runs <code>npm ci --ignore-scripts</code>, so a malicious lifecycle script cannot execute during the release build. ✅ <br>• <strong>CI uses OIDC, not a stored token</strong> - there is no <code>NPM_TOKEN</code> secret in GitHub for a malicious workflow step to steal. ✅ <br>• <code>package-lock.json</code> pins versions and integrity hashes - a <em>new</em> malicious version won't arrive silently, only on explicit update. ✅ <br>• <code>husky</code> is the only <code>prepare</code> hook and only writes <code>.git/hooks/</code>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Gaps - the workstation</strong></td>
<td>None of the above protects a maintainer running <code>npm install</code> <strong>locally</strong>. The lockfile pins <em>which</em> packages install, but if one of those pinned packages was <em>already</em> malicious when the lock was generated, or if a maintainer runs <code>npm update</code> / <code>npm install &lt;new-pkg&gt;</code>, the scripts run. <br><br><strong>The development environment has full read access to every credential the maintainer's user can read.</strong> That's the threat.</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Mitigations maintainers SHOULD adopt</strong> (in roughly descending order of effectiveness):</p>
<ol dir="auto">
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Don't keep a publish-capable npm token on your workstation.</strong>
Publishing happens via GitHub Actions OIDC. There is no workflow that requires <code>npm publish</code> from a laptop. If <code>~/.npmrc</code> has a token, it should be read-only or scoped to unrelated packages. <em>If there's nothing to steal, the attack is defanged.</em></p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Run <code>npm install</code> / <code>npm ci</code> with <code>--ignore-scripts</code> locally.</strong>
Add to a project-local <code>.npmrc</code>:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="ignore-scripts=true"><pre class="notranslate"><code>ignore-scripts=true
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Then explicitly run the one trusted script you need:
<code>npm rebuild husky &amp;&amp; npx husky</code>. The minor inconvenience of manually running known-good post-install steps is the price of not running thousands of unknown ones.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Develop in an isolated environment.</strong>
A devcontainer, VM, or sandbox profile that does not have:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><code>~/.ssh/</code> mounted (use a separate deploy key or SSH agent forwarding only when pushing)</li>
<li><code>~/.npmrc</code> with publish tokens</li>
<li><code>~/.config/gh/</code> with a <code>repo</code>-scoped GitHub token</li>
<li><code>~/.aws/</code>, <code>~/.config/gcloud/</code>, etc.</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">The dev environment should be able to read/write the repo working tree and reach the network for tests. Nothing else.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Use hardware-backed keys for GitHub.</strong>
FIDO2/WebAuthn for the GitHub account, and <code>sk-ssh-ed25519@openssh.com</code> for git push. A stolen <code>~/.ssh/id_ed25519_sk</code> is useless without the physical key. This converts "steal a file" into "steal a file AND a physical object."</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Audit lockfile diffs on dependency-update PRs as carefully as code.</strong>
A 4000-line <code>package-lock.json</code> diff hides a lot. Tooling: <code>npm diff</code>, <code>lockfile-lint</code>, Socket.dev's PR integration. Pay particular attention to new packages with install scripts (<code>hasInstallScript: true</code> in the lockfile).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Don't add dev dependencies casually.</strong>
Each one is a recurring trust decision delegated to a stranger. Prefer tools that can run via <code>npx</code> on demand (not in <code>node_modules</code>) or that are already in the tree.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">T-S3: Phishing → maintainer account takeover</h4><a id="user-content-t-s3-phishing--maintainer-account-takeover" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: T-S3: Phishing → maintainer account takeover" href="#t-s3-phishing--maintainer-account-takeover"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th></th>
<th></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td><strong>Description</strong></td>
<td>Maintainer receives a convincing email: <br>• "<em>npm security alert: your axios package has been flagged, log in to verify ownership</em>" → fake npm login → password + TOTP captured and replayed in real-time. <br>• "<em>GitHub: @axios has been added to a new organization, review access</em>" → fake GitHub OAuth consent → attacker app gets <code>repo</code> scope. <br>• Social: a "recruiter" asks the maintainer to clone and <code>npm install</code> a "take-home assignment" repo. <br><br>npm and GitHub credentials for axios maintainers have been <em>specifically targeted</em> by these campaigns in the past - this is not theoretical.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Likelihood</strong></td>
<td><strong>High.</strong> These campaigns are continuous.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Impact</strong></td>
<td>Critical. GitHub account → push tag → publish. npm account → publish directly.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Mitigations</strong></td>
<td>• npm 2FA is <strong>required</strong> for publish on the <code>axios</code> package. <br>• But: TOTP 2FA is <strong>phishable</strong> via real-time relay (Evilginx, Modlishka). <br>• OIDC publishing means there's no maintainer npm session involved in a normal release - this <em>narrows</em> the attack to GitHub. <br>• GitHub: maintainers should use <strong>WebAuthn/passkeys</strong>, which are origin-bound and cannot be relayed by a phishing proxy. TOTP is not sufficient for an account guarding a package this widely deployed.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Gaps</strong></td>
<td>• This is a <em>policy</em> control, not enforceable in the repo. The project cannot verify what 2FA method each maintainer uses. <br>• No documented "I think I've been phished" runbook (revoke sessions, rotate keys, audit recent tags, contact npm support).</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">T-S4: Compromised runtime dependency</h4><a id="user-content-t-s4-compromised-runtime-dependency" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: T-S4: Compromised runtime dependency" href="#t-s4-compromised-runtime-dependency"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th></th>
<th></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td><strong>Description</strong></td>
<td><code>follow-redirects</code>, <code>form-data</code>, or <code>proxy-from-env</code> ships a malicious version. Unlike T-S2, this code ends up <strong>in the published axios bundle / runtime</strong>, not just on maintainer machines. Every axios consumer runs it.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Likelihood</strong></td>
<td>Low (only 3 deps; all are mature, narrowly-scoped, and watched)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Impact</strong></td>
<td>Critical</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Mitigations</strong></td>
<td>• Three runtime deps total - minimal by design. <br>• <code>^</code> ranges in <code>package.json</code> mean consumers may get newer patch versions than the lockfile pins - this is intentional (consumers get security fixes) but means a malicious patch release of <code>follow-redirects</code> propagates without an axios release. <br>• <code>follow-redirects</code> is security-conscious and well-maintained; we track its advisories closely (multiple past axios releases were just <code>follow-redirects</code> bumps). <br>• Dependabot is configured (<code>.github/dependabot.yml</code>) for both npm and GitHub Actions, running weekly with grouped updates for production and development dependencies.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Gaps</strong></td>
<td>• No vendoring/inlining considered. The deps are small enough that vendoring is plausible but would forfeit upstream security fixes. Current judgment: not worth it.</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">T-S5: Build-output tampering (<code>dist/</code> ≠ <code>lib/</code>)</h4><a id="user-content-t-s5-build-output-tampering-dist--lib" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: T-S5: Build-output tampering (dist/ ≠ lib/)" href="#t-s5-build-output-tampering-dist--lib"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th></th>
<th></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td><strong>Description</strong></td>
<td>The published tarball contains a <code>dist/axios.min.js</code> that doesn't match what <code>rollup</code> would produce from <code>lib/</code>. Nobody reads minified bundles. A backdoor here is invisible to source review. <br><br>Vectors: a malicious dev-dep Rollup/Babel/Terser plugin injects code at build time (T-S2 applied to CI), or a maintainer with a compromised workstation accidentally publishes a tampered local build.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Likelihood</strong></td>
<td>Low</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Impact</strong></td>
<td>Critical</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Mitigations</strong></td>
<td>• Builds run <strong>only in CI</strong> as part of <code>publish.yml</code>, from a clean <code>npm ci --ignore-scripts</code> checkout. There is no "publish from laptop" path. ✅ <br>• <code>--ignore-scripts</code> means a malicious dev dep can't tamper with <code>node_modules</code> <em>before</em> the build, but it <strong>can</strong> still tamper <em>during</em> the build if it's a Rollup/Babel plugin - those run as part of <code>npm run build</code>, not as lifecycle scripts. <br>• npm provenance (<code>--provenance</code>) cryptographically attests <em>which workflow on which commit</em> produced the tarball. Consumers can verify with <code>npm audit signatures</code>. This proves the build ran in GitHub Actions on a known SHA - it does <strong>not</strong> prove the build is correct, only that it's traceable.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Gaps</strong></td>
<td>• The build is not currently <strong>reproducible</strong> in the strict sense - a third party cannot independently rebuild and get a byte-identical <code>dist/</code>. Timestamps, plugin ordering, and minifier nondeterminism would need to be locked down. <br>• No automated <code>dist/</code>-vs-rebuild diff in CI. This is the cheapest available improvement.</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">T-S6: Workflow file tampering</h4><a id="user-content-t-s6-workflow-file-tampering" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: T-S6: Workflow file tampering" href="#t-s6-workflow-file-tampering"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th></th>
<th></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td><strong>Description</strong></td>
<td>Attacker with write access (or a merged PR that wasn't reviewed carefully) modifies <code>.github/workflows/publish.yml</code> to also <code>curl</code> the OIDC token somewhere, or to add a step that patches <code>dist/</code> after the build.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Likelihood</strong></td>
<td>Low</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Impact</strong></td>
<td>Critical</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Mitigations</strong></td>
<td>• All actions are pinned to <strong>full commit SHAs</strong>, not tags - <code>actions/checkout@de0fac…</code> not <code>@v6</code>. A compromised action tag can't silently change behavior. ✅ <br>• <code>permissions:</code> are minimal (<code>contents: read</code>, <code>id-token: write</code>). <br>• <code>persist-credentials: false</code> on checkout - the build steps cannot push back to the repo. <br>• <code>zizmor</code> lints workflows on every PR. <br>• The <code>npm-publish</code> GitHub Environment can require designated reviewers before the job runs - a tampered workflow still pauses for human approval.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Gaps</strong></td>
<td>• No <code>CODEOWNERS</code> rule requiring extra scrutiny on <code>.github/workflows/**</code>. A workflow change can currently be approved by any single maintainer.</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">T-S7: Tag confusion / replay</h4><a id="user-content-t-s7-tag-confusion--replay" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: T-S7: Tag confusion / replay" href="#t-s7-tag-confusion--replay"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th></th>
<th></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td><strong>Description</strong></td>
<td>Attacker with write access force-pushes an existing tag to point at a malicious commit, or pushes <code>v1.99.99</code> so that a release is published out of band.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Likelihood</strong></td>
<td>Low (requires write access - assumed compromised at that point)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Impact</strong></td>
<td>High</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Mitigations</strong></td>
<td>• npm rejects re-publishing an existing version - re-tagging you cannot overwrite the published <code>1.15.0</code>. <br>• Provenance attestation records the commit SHA the tag pointed to <em>at publish time</em> - forensically verifiable. <br>• GitHub tag protection rules can prevent tag deletion/force-push.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Gaps</strong></td>
<td>A <em>new</em> malicious version (<code>v1.x.x</code>) is still publishable by anyone with tag-push rights - this collapses back into T-S3 (account security).</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">T-S8: Typosquatting / dependency confusion</h4><a id="user-content-t-s8-typosquatting--dependency-confusion" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: T-S8: Typosquatting / dependency confusion" href="#t-s8-typosquatting--dependency-confusion"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th></th>
<th></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td><strong>Description</strong></td>
<td>Attacker publishes <code>axois</code>, <code>axios-http</code>, <code>@axios/core</code>, etc., and waits for typos. Or publishes a package shadowing an internal name used in a consumer's monorepo.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Likelihood</strong></td>
<td>High (these packages already exist)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Impact</strong></td>
<td>Medium - affects confused consumers, not axios itself</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>In scope?</strong></td>
<td>Mostly out of scope; the axios project cannot police the npm namespace.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>Mitigations</strong></td>
<td>• npm has typosquat detection at publish time (imperfect). <br>• The <code>@axios/</code> npm scope is <strong>not owned</strong> by the project - <code>@axios/anything</code> can be registered by anyone. This is a gap, not a mitigation. <br>• Provenance gives consumers a way to verify they got the real thing.</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">3.6 Summary: Project Risk Posture</h3><a id="user-content-36-summary-project-risk-posture" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: 3.6 Summary: Project Risk Posture" href="#36-summary-project-risk-posture"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>Threat</th>
<th>Likelihood</th>
<th>Impact</th>
<th>Current Posture</th>
<th>Priority Gap</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>T-S1 Malicious PR</td>
<td>High</td>
<td>Critical</td>
<td>🟡 Adequate</td>
<td>Add CODEOWNERS for sensitive paths</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>T-S2 Dev-dep steals keys</strong></td>
<td><strong>Medium</strong></td>
<td><strong>Critical</strong></td>
<td><strong>🔴 Weak</strong></td>
<td><strong>Local <code>--ignore-scripts</code>; no publish tokens on workstations</strong></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>T-S3 Phishing</strong></td>
<td><strong>High</strong></td>
<td><strong>Critical</strong></td>
<td><strong>🟡 Partial</strong></td>
<td><strong>Mandate WebAuthn (not TOTP) for maintainer GitHub accounts</strong></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>T-S4 Runtime dep compromise</td>
<td>Low</td>
<td>Critical</td>
<td>🟢 Good</td>
<td>-</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>T-S5 Build tampering</td>
<td>Low</td>
<td>Critical</td>
<td>🟡 Adequate</td>
<td>Reproducible-build verification step</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>T-S6 Workflow tampering</td>
<td>Low</td>
<td>Critical</td>
<td>🟢 Good</td>
<td>CODEOWNERS on <code>.github/</code></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>T-S7 Tag replay</td>
<td>Low</td>
<td>High</td>
<td>🟢 Good</td>
<td>-</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>T-S8 Typosquat</td>
<td>High</td>
<td>Medium</td>
<td>⚪ Out of scope</td>
<td>-</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
<p dir="auto"><strong>The two threats most worth investing in are T-S2 and T-S3.</strong> Both target the maintainer rather than the code, both bypass every in-repo control, and both have well-understood, low-cost mitigations that are currently a matter of individual maintainer discipline rather than enforced policy.</p>
<hr>
<p dir="auto"><em>This document describes intent and current understanding. It does not constitute a security guarantee. To report a gap in the model itself, use the same private advisory channel as for code vulnerabilities.</em></p>

</react-app>




  </div>

</turbo-frame>

    </main>
  </div>

  </div>
